---
title: "ubuntu 14.04 server kvm nested virtualization guest microsoft server 2016 ver5"
date: 2016-07-11
forum: Virtualisation
---

### Post by hotsummer55 on 2016-07-11
I have ubuntu server 14.04.4  kernel 3.13.0-91-generic with kvm setup
I am trying to get nested virtualization to work
I have enabled nested on kernel boot by editing
/etc/default/grub
and adding
GRUB_CMDLINE_LINUX_DEFAULT="intel_iommu=on kvm-intel.nested=1"
The line 
kvm-intel.nested=1  enables nesting
then run 
update-grub
then reboot
I check this worked by[B][SIZE=3]
# cat /sys/module/kvm_intel/parameters/nested[/SIZE][/B][B]
Y[/B]
[B][SIZE=3]or
# systool -m kvm_intel -v   | grep -i nested
    nested              = "Y"
# [/SIZE]
This worked
I create a vm and the edited the xml file adding in cpu section
  <cpu mode='host-passthrough'>
  <feature policy='require' name='vmx'/>
  </cpu>

I then booted and in windows server 2016 ver 5 i checked that vmx was enabled by running
coreinfo
and it is
before it was enabled the setup in microsoft server would complain about vmx not enable and it does not complain now


The problem is now server 2016 preview  5 is reporting error
Hyper-V cannot be installed because virtualization support is not enabled in the BIOS

I cant find any info about this and seabios
I suspect seabios is reporting incorrect info to windows
Is there any setting I can change in seabios

Has anybody any info on this or suggestion .I would like to play with windows server 2016 hypervisor im afraid and enabling this would be handy.I still have to learn windows stuff


see error below in windows

### Post by MAFoElffen on 2016-07-15
My posts from yesterday are gone... Posted them just before the forum went down yesterday, and they installed it back from scratch.

What I had said (summarized version with screen shots) was that 

From my real-hardware server host, with base OS Win Server 2k12r2 DataCenter, running hyper-v:
 - With VM guest Win Server 2k16pv5 running hyper-v, I can also install a nested Win Server Win2k16pv5 Guest.


From my real-hardware server host, with base OS Ubuntu Server 16.04 LTS, running KVM:
 - With Ubuntu Server 16.04 guest running KVM, I can run a Win Server 2k16pv5 guest.
 - With CENTOS Server 7.0 guest running KVM, I can run a Win Server 2k16pv5 guest.
 - With a Solaris 11.2 guest , running OVM, I can runn a Win Server 2k16pv5 guest.
 - *** With a Win Server 2k16pv5 guest, I cannot install Hyper-V. But if I run Intel's CPU ID tools wthin that guest, it says that Virtualization Technology is seen as enabled in that guest. But hyper-v will not install, with the same erro you are getting.

I get the same with mY real-hardware server host, with base OS Ubuntu server 16.04, running Xen, doing nesting with Linux hosts and Win Server 2k16pv5. I haven't tried it from vSphere yet & 2k16pv5, but that does not resemble what you are asking about.

I'm thinking it has to do with something between Win Server 2l16 pv4 and pv5. and something they are looking for in their requirements for installing hyper-v(???). The same guest is seeing itself as being virtual technologies enabled, but by their feature installation, then not seeing something.

As I'm seeing that happen also for Xen, I'll ask my son if he could report it to upstream to MS, as he is a System Engineer, using Citrix for over 200 MS Win Servers, so is on both companies paid support contracts.

### Post by aeltester on 2016-08-16
wow. after three days of constant fiddling, here i stumbled acress

<cpu mode='host-passthrough'>
<feature policy='require' name='vmx'/>
</cpu>

which is the only thing that seems to work other than core2duo.

Many thanks!

---
